Let me also write a comprehensive summary of the fix.\n\nSummary of the fix:\n1. Problem: When using `{% include \"child.html\" only %}` inside a `{% for %}` loop, the child template could access parent context variables like `forloop.counter`, despite using the \"only\" keyword for context isolation.\n\n2. Root cause: When `IncludeNode.render()` called `template.render(context.new(values))` to create an isolated context, it only reset the main context dicts but not the RenderContext. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01YXnRP8zrehyrqdMbvSbjg7","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_0134h4oxFLUhenLRpU5KLo9o","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/FIX_SUMMARY.md","content":"# Django Template Context Isolation Fix - SEC-0472\n\n## Vulnerability Summary\n\n**Finding ID:** SEC-0472\n**Severity:** Medium\n**Category:** Information Leakage / Context Isolation Bypass\n\nDjango's template system provides context isolation through the `{% include \"template.html\" only %}` syntax. However, special variables injected by template tags (particularly loop variables like `forloop`) were leaking into isolated included templates, violating the isolation contract.\n\n## Proof of Concept\n\n```django\n{% for item in items %}\n  {% include \"child.html\" only %}\n{% endfor %}\n```\n\nIn `child.html`:\n```django\n{{ forloop.counter }}  <!-- Should be undefined with \"only\", but renders! -->\n```\n\nDue to the vulnerability, `{{ forloop.counter }}` would render even with the `only` keyword.\n\n## Root Cause Analysis\n\nWhen `IncludeNode.render()` processed an isolated include (with the `only` keyword), it called:\n```python\nreturn template.render(context.new(values))\n```\n\nThe `context.new()` method was intended to create a completely isolated context by:\n1. Creating a shallow copy of the context object\n2. Resetting the main context dicts (`BaseContext._reset_dicts()`)\n\nHowever, it did NOT reset the `render_context`, which is also copied during context creation. The `render_context` maintains a `dicts` list that is shallow-copied, potentially allowing references to parent context state to persist.\n\n## The Fix\n\nModified `/workspace/django/template/context.py` by overriding the `new()` method in the `Context` class:\n\n```python\ndef new(self, values=None):\n    \"\"\"\n    Return a new context with the same properties, but with only the\n    values given in 'values' stored. For the Context class, this also\n    creates a fresh RenderContext to ensure complete isolation.\n    \"\"\"\n    new_context = super().new(values)\n    # Create a fresh RenderContext to prevent state leakage from parent context\n    new_context.render_context = RenderContext()\n    return new_context\n```\n\n### Why This Fix Works\n\n1. **Main Context Isolation**: The parent class's `new()` method still resets the main dicts, ensuring variables don't leak.\n\n2. **Render Context Isolation**: By creating a completely fresh `RenderContext()`, we ensure no state from the parent template rendering (like loop iteration variables) can leak into the child template.\n\n3. **Cascading Benefits**:\n   - `RequestContext.new()` calls `super().new()`, so it automatically gets the fix\n   - Inclusion tags (`django.template.library`) that use `context.new()` also benefit\n   - All existing callers of `context.new()` automatically get proper isolation\n\n## Impact\n\n### What Was Fixed\n- Isolated includes no longer leak parent context variables (including loop variables)\n- Inclusion tags get proper context isolation\n- Non-isolated includes continue to work correctly (they use `context.push()`, not `context.new()`)\n\n### What Still Works\n- Normal template includes without `only` keyword still pass full parent context\n- Template inheritance via `{% extends %}` is unaffected\n- All existing context functionality is preserved\n\n## Files Modified\n\n- `/workspace/django/template/context.py` - Added `new()` method to `Context` class\n\n## Files Examined (Audit Trail)\n\n- `django/template/loader_tags.py` - IncludeNode implementation\n- `django/template/context.py` - Context and RenderContext implementation\n- `django/template/base.py` - Template rendering logic\n- `django/template/defaulttags.py` - ForNode implementation (to understand loop variables)\n- `django/template/library.py` - Inclusion tags that also use context.new()\n\n## Testing\n\nThe fix can be verified by creating a template with a for loop that includes an isolated template and checking that loop variables are not accessible in the isolated template.\n\nExample test case:\n```python\n# Parent template with for loop\n{% for item in items %}\n  {% include \"child.html\" only %}\n{% endfor %}\n\n# Child template (should not have access to forloop)\n{{ forloop.counter }}  # Should render as empty/undefined\n```\n\n## Security Implications\n\nThis fix closes an information disclosure vulnerability that could have been exploited in multi-tenant template rendering scenarios to leak sensitive variables from one tenant's context to another tenant's included templates.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":0,"cache_creation_input_tokens":615,"cache_read_input_tokens":102694,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":615},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"10dcf534-74ee-4112-a630-08698cb8e115","uuid":"46af5e10-1422-4092-ab60-3df4d9dcc712"}

However, special variables injected by template tags (particularly loop variables like `forloop`) were leaking into isolated included templates, violating the isolation contract.\n\n## Proof of Concept\n\n```django\n{% for item in items %}\n  {% include \"child.html\" only %}\n{% endfor %}\n```\n\nIn `child.html`:\n```django\n{{ forloop.counter }}  <!-- Should be undefined with \"only\", but renders! -->\n```\n\nDue to the vulnerability, `{{ forloop.counter }}` would render even with the `only` keyword.\n\n## Root Cause Analysis\n\nWhen `IncludeNode.render()` processed an isolated include (with the `only` keyword), it called:\n```python\nreturn template.render(context.new(values))\n```\n\nThe `context.new()` method was intended to create a completely isolated context by:\n1. Creating a shallow copy of the context object\n2. Resetting the main context dicts (`BaseContext._reset_dicts()`)\n\nHowever, it did NOT reset the `render_context`, which is also copied during context creation. The `render_context` maintains a `dicts` list that is shallow-copied, potentially allowing references to parent context state to persist.\n\n## The Fix\n\nModified `/workspace/django/template/context.py` by overriding the `new()` method in the `Context` class:\n\n```python\ndef new(self, values=None):\n    \"\"\"\n    Return a new context with the same properties, but with only the\n    values given in 'values' stored. For the Context class, this also\n    creates a fresh RenderContext to ensure complete isolation.\n    \"\"\"\n    new_context = super().new(values)\n    # Create a fresh RenderContext to prevent state leakage from parent context\n    new_context.render_context = RenderContext()\n    return new_context\n```\n\n### Why This Fix Works\n\n1. **Main Context Isolation**: The parent class's `new()` method still resets the main dicts, ensuring variables don't leak.\n\n2. **Render Context Isolation**: By creating a completely fresh `RenderContext()`, we ensure no state from the parent template rendering (like loop iteration variables) can leak into the child template.\n\n3. **Cascading Benefits**:\n   - `RequestContext.new()` calls `super().new()`, so it automatically gets the fix\n   - Inclusion tags (`django.template.library`) that use `context.new()` also benefit\n   - All existing callers of `context.new()` automatically get proper isolation\n\n## Impact\n\n### What Was Fixed\n- Isolated includes no longer leak parent context variables (including loop variables)\n- Inclusion tags get proper context isolation\n- Non-isolated includes continue to work correctly (they use `context.push()`, not `context.new()`)\n\n### What Still Works\n- Normal template includes without `only` keyword still pass full parent context\n- Template inheritance via `{% extends %}` is unaffected\n- All existing context functionality is preserved\n\n## Files Modified\n\n- `/workspace/django/template/context.py` - Added `new()` method to `Context` class\n\n## Files Examined (Audit Trail)\n\n- `django/template/loader_tags.py` - IncludeNode implementation\n- `django/template/context.py` - Context and RenderContext implementation\n- `django/template/base.py` - Template rendering logic\n- `django/template/defaulttags.py` - ForNode implementation (to understand loop variables)\n- `django/template/library.py` - Inclusion tags that also use context.new()\n\n## Testing\n\nThe fix can be verified by creating a template with a for loop that includes an isolated template and checking that loop variables are not accessible in the isolated template.\n\nExample test case:\n```python\n# Parent template with for loop\n{% for item in items %}\n  {% include \"child.html\" only %}\n{% endfor %}\n\n# Child template (should not have access to forloop)\n{{ forloop.counter }}  # Should render as empty/undefined\n```\n\n## Security Implications\n\nThis fix closes an information disclosure vulnerability that could have been exploited in multi-tenant template rendering scenarios to leak sensitive variables from one tenant's context to another tenant's included templates.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

For the Context class, this also\n    creates a fresh RenderContext to ensure complete isolation.\n    \"\"\"\n    new_context = super().new(values)\n    # Create a fresh RenderContext to prevent state leakage from parent context\n    new_context.render_context = RenderContext()\n    return new_context\n```\n\n## How the Fix Works\n\n1.
